The Three Rational Judgments
Sanusi enumerates the three rational judgments and defines each.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of rational judgment as confined to three categories—necessary, impossible, and possible—and how these categories function as the foundation of all theological reasoning in kalam.

Core Idea
The three rational judgments are the basic categories of the mind's reasoning about existence.

This lesson introduces the foundational classification of rational judgments in Islamic theology. Before we can discuss what is true about Allah, we need a shared vocabulary for what the mind can conceive as necessary, impossible, or possible. Sanusi begins by defining these three categories, which will underpin all subsequent arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage carefully, then read the English translation. Notice how concise and precise the definitions are.
The passage uses technical terms that will recur throughout the course.
2
Identify the three categories and their definitions
Pick out each of the three categories—necessary (الواجب), impossible (المستحيل), possible (الجائز)—and note their definitions as given by Sanusi.
Each definition revolves around what the mind can or cannot conceive.
3
Reflect on why only three categories
Ask yourself why these three categories are exhaustive. The mind either cannot conceive non-existence, cannot conceive existence, or can conceive both.
This exhaustive division is key to all kalam reasoning.
4
Consider application to Allah's attributes
Think about how this classification will be used: for example, existence is necessary for Allah, non-existence is impossible, and actions like creating are possible.
This connects the lesson to the broader purpose of kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعْلَمْ أَنَّ الْحُكْمَ الْعَقْلِيَّ يَنْحَصِرُ فِي ثَلَاثَةِ أَقْسَامٍ: الْوُجُوبِ، وَالْإِسْتِحَالَةِ، وَالْجَوَازِ. فَالْوَاجِبُ مَا لَا يُتَصَوَّرُ فِي الْعَقْلِ عَدَمُهُ، وَالْمُسْتَحِيلُ مَا لَا يُتَصَوَّرُ فِي الْعَقْلِ وُجُودُهُ، وَالْجَائِزُ مَا يَصِحُ فِي الْعَقْلِ وُجُودُهُ وَعَدَمُهُ.
Know that the rational judgment is confined to three categories: the necessary, the impossible, and the possible. The necessary is that whose non-existence is not conceivable in the mind, the impossible is that whose existence is not conceivable in the mind, and the possible is that whose existence and non-existence are both valid in the mind.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage defines the three rational judgments (الأحكام العقلية) which are foundational in kalam. It states that rational judgment is limited to three types: necessary (وجوب), impossible (استحالة), and possible (جواز). Each is defined by what the intellect can conceive or not conceive. The necessary is that whose non-existence is impossible to conceive (i.e., it must exist). The impossible is that whose existence is impossible to conceive. The possible is that which the intellect accepts may either exist or not exist. This classification is the basis for all discussions about God's attributes and actions: what is necessary for God, what is impossible for Him, and what is possible for Him.

Key Terms
الحكم العقلي
الواجب
المستحيل
الجائز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'possible' in kalam means contingent in the sense of having equal probability, like a coin toss.
Correction: The text defines possible as what the intellect deems equally valid for existence and non-existence, independent of external reality. It is a rational judgment, not a statistical probability.

Checkpoint
What is the definition of the impossible (المستحيل) in rational judgment?
A) that whose non-existence is not conceivable
B) that whose existence is not conceivable
C) that whose existence and non-existence are both conceivable
D) that which cannot be known

Key Takeaway
The three rational judgments—necessary, impossible, and possible—are the foundational categories for all reasoning about Allah in kalam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider the most fundamental belief you hold, is it truly necessary in the sense that your mind cannot conceive its non-existence, or is it merely possible? How does that affect the certainty of your faith?
?
Have you ever assumed something about Allah was impossible (like forgiving a specific sin of yours) when this passage says the impossible is only what the mind cannot conceive of existing at all? Will you let this truth change how you view His mercy today?
?
You exist as a possible being — you could have not existed. Does that realization humble you enough to live every moment in gratitude to the Necessary Being who chose to bring you into existence?

God's Actions Regarding Possibles are Morally Neutral
Sanusi presents a proof that God's actions are morally neutral regarding possibles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that God's actions towards possible things are neither obligatory nor impossible, but permissible.

Core Idea
If God were obligated, possibles would cease to be possible.

Sanusi now turns to a crucial point: are God's actions constrained by moral necessity? Using simple modal logic, he shows that if any act were required or forbidden for God by reason, the very category of possibility would collapse. This lesson unpacks that proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise style: a single conditional sentence and a concluding remark.
2
Understand the conditional argument
The passage presents a conditional: if any action were obligatory or impossible for God by reason, then the possible would become obligatory or impossible. Ask yourself why that conclusion is problematic.
The key is that the possible is defined as what is neither necessary nor impossible.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Sanusi concludes that such a transformation is 'not rationally conceivable'. Reflect on what this tells us about God's freedom and the nature of possibility.
This preserves God's complete freedom regarding creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا بُرْهَانُ كَوْنِ فِعْلِ الْمُمْكِنَاتِ أَوْ تَرْكِهَا جَائِزاً فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى، فَلِأَنَّهُ لَوْ وَجَبَ عَلَيْهِ تَعَالَى شَيْءٌ مِنْهَا عَقْلاً، أَوِ اسْتَحَالَ عَقْلاً لَانْقَلَبَ الْمُمْكِنُ وَاجِباً أَوْ مُسْتَحِيلاً. وَذَلِكَ لَا يُعْقَلُ.
And as for the proof that the doing or leaving of possible things is permissible with respect to Him, exalted is He, it is because if any of them were obligatory upon Him, exalted is He, by reason, or impossible by reason, the possible would become obligatory or impossible. And that is not rationally conceivable.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage proves that God's actions regarding possible things (mumkinat) are morally neutral (ja'iz), meaning they are neither obligatory (wajib) nor impossible (mustahil) upon Him. Sanusi argues that if an act, such as creating the world, were rationally obligatory or impossible for God, then the very concept of possibility would be contradicted: a possible thing would turn into an obligatory or impossible one. This is rationally inconceivable because possibility is a distinct modal category. Therefore, God's action concerning possibles is free and unconstrained.

Key Terms
مُمْكِن
جَائِز
وَاجِب
مُسْتَحِيل
عَقْل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's mercy obligates Him to create the world.
Correction: Sanusi shows that if an action were obligatory for God by reason, the possible would become necessary, which is rationally inconceivable. Thus, God is not obligated by any external factor.

Checkpoint
What would happen if an action were obligatory or impossible for God by reason?
A) The possible would become either obligatory or impossible, which is inconceivable.
B) God would be constrained, which is acceptable.
C) The action would become necessary for the world.
D) Nothing, because God is above reason.

Key Takeaway
God's actions regarding possible things are morally neutral, because any obligation or impossibility would contradict the nature of possibility itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever catch yourself feeling that God owes you something—a specific outcome, a certain blessing, or a particular path in life? How does this lesson challenge that feeling today?
?
If God's actions regarding all possible worlds are morally neutral, then He was free not to create you. Does that thought trouble you or free you? How does it affect your gratitude and trust in His wisdom?
?
When you face hardship, do you silently accuse God of failing an obligation to you? What would it mean for your relationship with Him to truly believe that He never owes you anything, and that everything He does is a gift?

The Three Rational Judgments
Sanusi states the three rational judgments regarding Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three rational categories (wājib, mustaḥīl, jā’iz) that form the foundation of all knowledge about Allah in Islamic theology.

Core Idea
The three rational judgments are the logical grammar of all kalam.

Sanusi begins his theological exposition by establishing the three rational categories every responsible Muslim must know about Allah. These categories—necessary, impossible, and permissible—are the basic tools for reasoning about the Divine. This passage lays the groundwork for all subsequent theological discussions.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening sentence
Read the Arabic passage once. It is a single sentence defining the three categories. Notice the concise style.
The sentence begins with 'بِسْمِ اللَّهِ'.
2
Identify the three categories
The passage explicitly lists three terms: wājib (necessary), mustaḥīl (impossible), jā’iz (permissible). Mark each one in your mind.
These are the three rational judgments (al-aqsām al-thalātha).
3
Reflect on their role
Ask yourself: why are these three categories the first thing a student of kalam learns? They are the framework for all theological attributes.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بِسْمِ اللَّهِ. الْأَقْسَامُ الثَّلَاثَةُ الَّتِي يَجِبُ عَلَى الْمُكَلَّفِ مَعْرِفَتُهَا فِي حَقِّ مَوْلَانَا جَلَّ وَعَزَّ، وَهِيَ مَا يَجِبُ فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى، وَمَا يَسْتَحِيلُ، وَمَا يَجُوزُ. وَأَمَّا قَوْلُنَا مُحَمَّدٌ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَيَدْخُلُ فِيهِ الْإِيمَانُ بِسَائِرِ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ وَالْمَلَائِكَةِ وَالْكُتُبِ السَّمَاوِيَّةِ وَالْيَوْمِ الْآخِرِ، لِأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ جَاءَ بِتَصْدِيقِ جَمِيعِ ذَلِكَ كُلِّهِ، وَيُؤْخَذُ مِنْهُ وُجُوبُ صِدْقِ الرُّسُلِ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ وَاسْتِحَالَةُ الْكَذِبِ عَلَيْهِمْ، وَإِلَّا لَمْ يَكُونُوا رُسُلًا أُمَنَاءَ لِمَوْلَانَا الْعَالِمِ بِالْخَفِيَّاتِ جَلَّ وَعَزَّ، وَاسْتِحَالَةُ فِعْلِ الْمَنْهِيَّاتِ كُلِّهَا لِأَنَّهُمْ أُرْسِلُوا لِيُعَلِّمُوا النَّاسَ بِأَقْوَالِهِمْ وَأَفْعَالِهِمْ وَسُكُونِهِمْ، فَيَلْزَمُ أَنْ لَا يَكُونَ فِي جَمِيعِهَا مُخَالَفَةٌ لِأَمْرِ مَوْلَانَا جَلَّ وَعَزَّ الَّذِي اخْتَارَهُمْ عَلَى جَمِيعِ خَلْقِهِ وَأَمَّنَهُمْ عَلَى سِرِّ وَحْيِهِ، وَيُؤْخَذُ مِنْهُ جَوَازُ الْأَعْرَاضِ الْبَشَرِيَّةِ عَلَيْهِمْ، إِذْ ذَاكَ لَا يَقْدَحُ فِي رِسَالَتِهِمْ، وَعُلُوِّ مَنْزِلَتِهِمْ عِنْدَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى بَلْ ذَاكَ مِمَّا يَزِيدُ فِيهَا، فَقَدْ بَانَ لَكَ تَضَمَّنُ كَلِمَتَيِ الشَّهَادَةِ مَعَ قِلَّةِ حُرُوفِهَا لِجَمِيعِ مَا يَجِبُ عَلَى الْمُكَلَّفِ مَعْرِفَتُهُ مِنْ عَقَائِدِ الْإِيمَانِ فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى وَفِي حَقِّ رُسُلِهِ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ، وَلَعَلَّهَا لِاخْتِصَارِهَا مَعَ اشْتِمَالِهَا عَلَى مَا ذَكَرْنَاهُ جَعَلَهَا الشَّرْعُ تَرْجَمَةً عَلَى مَا فِي الْقَلْبِ مِنَ الْإِسْلَامِ، وَلَمْ يَقْبَلْ مِنْ أَحَدٍ الْإِيمَانَ إِلَّا بِهَا، فَعَلَى الْعَاقِلِ أَنْ يُكْثِرَ مِنْ ذِكْرِهَا مُسْتَحْضِرًا لِمَا احْتَوَتْ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ عَقَائِدِ الْإِيمَانِ حَتَّى يَمْتَزِجَ مَعْنَاهَا بِلَحْمِهِ وَدَمِهِ فَإِنَّهُ يَرَى لَهَا مِنَ الْأَسْرَارِ وَالْعَجَائِبِ إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى مَا لَا يَدْخُلُ تَحْتَ حَصْرٍ، وَبِاللَّهِ التَّوْفِيقُ لَا رَبَّ غَيْرُهُ وَلَا مَعْبُودَ سِوَاهُ، نَسْأَلُهُ سُبْحَانَهُ وَتَعَالَى أَنْ يَجْعَلَنَا وَأَحِبَّتَنَا عِنْدَ الْمَوْتِ نَاطِقِينَ بِكَلِمَةِ الشَّهَادَةِ عَالِمِينَ بِهَا، وَصَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَى سَيِّدِنَا مُحَمَّدٍ، كُلَّمَا ذَكَرَهُ الذَّاكِرُونَ وَغَفَلَ عَنْ ذِكْرِهِ الْغَافِلُونَ، وَرَضِيَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى عَنْ أَصْحَابِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ أَجْمَعِينَ وَالتَّابِعِينَ لَهُمْ بِإِحْسَانٍ إِلَى يَوْمِ الدِّينِ، وَسَلَامٌ عَلَى الْمُرْسَلِينَ، وَالْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ.
In the name of Allah. The three divisions that are obligatory for the legally responsible person (al-mukallaf) to know concerning our Master, may He be glorified and exalted, are: what is necessary (wājib) in His right, the Exalted, what is impossible (mustaḥīl), and what is permissible (jā’iz). And as for our statement 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace,' it includes belief in all the prophets, angels, heavenly books, and the Last Day, because he, peace and blessings be upon him, came affirming all of that. And from this is derived the necessity of the truthfulness of the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, and the impossibility of lying for them, otherwise they would not be trustworthy messengers for our Master, the Knower of hidden things, may He be glorified and exalted, and the impossibility of committing all forbidden actions because they were sent to teach people by their sayings, actions, and states, so it is necessary that there be no contradiction in all of that to the command of our Master, may He be glorified and exalted, who chose them over all His creation and entrusted them with the secret of His revelation. And from this is derived the permissibility of human accidental attributes (al-a‘rāḍ al-bashariyya) for them, for that does not detract from their messengership, but rather increases their rank with Allah, the Exalted. So it has become clear to you that the two testimonies, despite the fewness of their letters, contain all that is obligatory for the legally responsible person to know of the beliefs of faith concerning Him, the Exalted, and concerning His messengers, peace and blessings be upon them. And perhaps it is for their conciseness, with their inclusion of what we have mentioned, that the Sacred Law made them the expression (tarjama) of what is in the heart of Islam, and did not accept faith from anyone except by them. So it is upon the intelligent person (al-‘āqil) to repeat them frequently, keeping in mind the beliefs of faith they contain, until its meaning mixes with his flesh and blood, for he will see for them, if Allah wills, secrets and wonders beyond enumeration. And with Allah is success; there is no lord besides Him, and no worshipped other than Him. We ask Him, glorified and exalted, to make us and those we love at the time of death utterers of the testimony (kalimat al-shahāda), knowing it. May Allah bless our master Muhammad, whenever those who remember remember him and those who forget are heedless of his remembrance, and may Allah be pleased with all the companions of the Messenger of Allah and those who follow them in excellence until the Day of Judgment, and peace be upon the messengers, and praise be to Allah, the Lord of the worlds.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a combined classification and exposition. It begins by stating the three rational categories (wājib, mustaḥīl, jā’iz) that every responsible Muslim must know regarding Allah. Then it turns to the second testimony, showing that belief in Muhammad’s messengership entails belief in all previous prophets, angels, scriptures, and the Last Day, because Muhammad confirmed them. From this, the author deduces three things about prophets: (1) they must be truthful and cannot lie, otherwise they would not be trustworthy; (2) they are sinless—they cannot commit forbidden actions because they are models for teaching; (3) they may experience human accidents (like eating, illness) as these do not harm their status. After deriving these points, the author marvels at the comprehensiveness of the two testimonies despite their brevity. He explains that Islamic law made them the expression of inner faith and does not accept belief without them. He concludes by urging the intelligent believer to recite them frequently with mindfulness of their meanings, so that faith becomes deeply ingrained. The passage ends with a prayer for a good death uttering the shahada with knowledge, and with salutations and praise.

Key Terms
الأقسام الثلاثة
واجب
مستحيل
جائز

A) Wājib, mustaḥīl, jā’iz
B) Wujūd, qidam, baqā’
C) Tawḥīd, nubuwwa, ma‘ād
D) Īmān, islām, iḥsān

Key Takeaway
The three rational judgments are the essential categories for understanding Islamic theology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You now know that learning these three rational judgments is a religious obligation upon every legally responsible person. Have you ever treated this knowledge as a mere intellectual curiosity rather than a required duty? What would change in your daily awareness of Allah if you consciously applied these categories to everything you think or say about Him?
?
The source says these divisions are 'concerning our Master'—they are about your Lord. When was the last time you paused to check whether a thought or belief about Allah fit under wājib, mustaḥīl, or jā’iz? If you haven't, what is holding you back from making this a regular spiritual practice starting today?
?
You have just read that the mukallaf must know all three categories. Do you know them well enough to explain them to someone else? If not, what concrete step will you take this week to master them—not just memorize the terms but truly internalize their meaning for your relationship with Allah?

Rational Judgments
intermediate
6 min
The Comprehensive Second Testimony
Sanusi explains the implications of the second testimony.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the second testimony (Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah) implicitly includes belief in all prophets, angels, books, and the Last Day, and what this implies about the characteristics of prophets.

Core Idea
The second testimony is a concise summary of all prophetic teachings.

Sanusi shows that testifying to Muhammad's messengership is not limited to one prophet; it entails acceptance of everything he confirmed, which includes all previous prophets, angels, scriptures, and the Hereafter. From this, he derives three essential characteristics of prophets: truthfulness, sinlessness, and the permissibility of human attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the second testimony
Read the Arabic passage carefully from the start of the second testimony discussion. Notice how the author links belief in Muhammad to belief in all previous revelations.
The passage begins with 'وَأَمَّا قَوْلُنَا مُحَمَّدٌ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ'.
2
Note the inclusions
Identify the four things that belief in Muhammad's messengership includes: prophets, angels, books, Last Day.
The text says 'يَدْخُلُ فِيهِ الْإِيمَانُ بِسَائِرِ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ وَالْمَلَائِكَةِ وَالْكُتُبِ السَّمَاوِيَّةِ وَالْيَوْمِ الْآخِرِ'.
3
Derive the three prophetic attributes
The author then deduces three properties: (1) truthfulness and impossibility of lying, (2) impossibility of committing forbidden acts, (3) permissibility of human accidents. List them and understand the reasoning.
Each is introduced with 'يُؤْخَذُ مِنْهُ'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بِسْمِ اللَّهِ. الْأَقْسَامُ الثَّلَاثَةُ الَّتِي يَجِبُ عَلَى الْمُكَلَّفِ مَعْرِفَتُهَا فِي حَقِّ مَوْلَانَا جَلَّ وَعَزَّ، وَهِيَ مَا يَجِبُ فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى، وَمَا يَسْتَحِيلُ، وَمَا يَجُوزُ. وَأَمَّا قَوْلُنَا مُحَمَّدٌ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَيَدْخُلُ فِيهِ الْإِيمَانُ بِسَائِرِ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ وَالْمَلَائِكَةِ وَالْكُتُبِ السَّمَاوِيَّةِ وَالْيَوْمِ الْآخِرِ، لِأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ جَاءَ بِتَصْدِيقِ جَمِيعِ ذَلِكَ كُلِّهِ، وَيُؤْخَذُ مِنْهُ وُجُوبُ صِدْقِ الرُّسُلِ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ وَاسْتِحَالَةُ الْكَذِبِ عَلَيْهِمْ، وَإِلَّا لَمْ يَكُونُوا رُسُلًا أُمَنَاءَ لِمَوْلَانَا الْعَالِمِ بِالْخَفِيَّاتِ جَلَّ وَعَزَّ، وَاسْتِحَالَةُ فِعْلِ الْمَنْهِيَّاتِ كُلِّهَا لِأَنَّهُمْ أُرْسِلُوا لِيُعَلِّمُوا النَّاسَ بِأَقْوَالِهِمْ وَأَفْعَالِهِمْ وَسُكُونِهِمْ، فَيَلْزَمُ أَنْ لَا يَكُونَ فِي جَمِيعِهَا مُخَالَفَةٌ لِأَمْرِ مَوْلَانَا جَلَّ وَعَزَّ الَّذِي اخْتَارَهُمْ عَلَى جَمِيعِ خَلْقِهِ وَأَمَّنَهُمْ عَلَى سِرِّ وَحْيِهِ، وَيُؤْخَذُ مِنْهُ جَوَازُ الْأَعْرَاضِ الْبَشَرِيَّةِ عَلَيْهِمْ، إِذْ ذَاكَ لَا يَقْدَحُ فِي رِسَالَتِهِمْ، وَعُلُوِّ مَنْزِلَتِهِمْ عِنْدَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى بَلْ ذَاكَ مِمَّا يَزِيدُ فِيهَا، فَقَدْ بَانَ لَكَ تَضَمَّنُ كَلِمَتَيِ الشَّهَادَةِ مَعَ قِلَّةِ حُرُوفِهَا لِجَمِيعِ مَا يَجِبُ عَلَى الْمُكَلَّفِ مَعْرِفَتُهُ مِنْ عَقَائِدِ الْإِيمَانِ فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى وَفِي حَقِّ رُسُلِهِ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ، وَلَعَلَّهَا لِاخْتِصَارِهَا مَعَ اشْتِمَالِهَا عَلَى مَا ذَكَرْنَاهُ جَعَلَهَا الشَّرْعُ تَرْجَمَةً عَلَى مَا فِي الْقَلْبِ مِنَ الْإِسْلَامِ، وَلَمْ يَقْبَلْ مِنْ أَحَدٍ الْإِيمَانَ إِلَّا بِهَا، فَعَلَى الْعَاقِلِ أَنْ يُكْثِرَ مِنْ ذِكْرِهَا مُسْتَحْضِرًا لِمَا احْتَوَتْ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ عَقَائِدِ الْإِيمَانِ حَتَّى يَمْتَزِجَ مَعْنَاهَا بِلَحْمِهِ وَدَمِهِ فَإِنَّهُ يَرَى لَهَا مِنَ الْأَسْرَارِ وَالْعَجَائِبِ إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى مَا لَا يَدْخُلُ تَحْتَ حَصْرٍ، وَبِاللَّهِ التَّوْفِيقُ لَا رَبَّ غَيْرُهُ وَلَا مَعْبُودَ سِوَاهُ، نَسْأَلُهُ سُبْحَانَهُ وَتَعَالَى أَنْ يَجْعَلَنَا وَأَحِبَّتَنَا عِنْدَ الْمَوْتِ نَاطِقِينَ بِكَلِمَةِ الشَّهَادَةِ عَالِمِينَ بِهَا، وَصَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَى سَيِّدِنَا مُحَمَّدٍ، كُلَّمَا ذَكَرَهُ الذَّاكِرُونَ وَغَفَلَ عَنْ ذِكْرِهِ الْغَافِلُونَ، وَرَضِيَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى عَنْ أَصْحَابِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ أَجْمَعِينَ وَالتَّابِعِينَ لَهُمْ بِإِحْسَانٍ إِلَى يَوْمِ الدِّينِ، وَسَلَامٌ عَلَى الْمُرْسَلِينَ، وَالْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ.
In the name of Allah. The three divisions that are obligatory for the legally responsible person (al-mukallaf) to know concerning our Master, may He be glorified and exalted, are: what is necessary (wājib) in His right, the Exalted, what is impossible (mustaḥīl), and what is permissible (jā’iz). And as for our statement 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace,' it includes belief in all the prophets, angels, heavenly books, and the Last Day, because he, peace and blessings be upon him, came affirming all of that. And from this is derived the necessity of the truthfulness of the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, and the impossibility of lying for them, otherwise they would not be trustworthy messengers for our Master, the Knower of hidden things, may He be glorified and exalted, and the impossibility of committing all forbidden actions because they were sent to teach people by their sayings, actions, and states, so it is necessary that there be no contradiction in all of that to the command of our Master, may He be glorified and exalted, who chose them over all His creation and entrusted them with the secret of His revelation. And from this is derived the permissibility of human accidental attributes (al-a‘rāḍ al-bashariyya) for them, for that does not detract from their messengership, but rather increases their rank with Allah, the Exalted. So it has become clear to you that the two testimonies, despite the fewness of their letters, contain all that is obligatory for the legally responsible person to know of the beliefs of faith concerning Him, the Exalted, and concerning His messengers, peace and blessings be upon them. And perhaps it is for their conciseness, with their inclusion of what we have mentioned, that the Sacred Law made them the expression (tarjama) of what is in the heart of Islam, and did not accept faith from anyone except by them. So it is upon the intelligent person (al-‘āqil) to repeat them frequently, keeping in mind the beliefs of faith they contain, until its meaning mixes with his flesh and blood, for he will see for them, if Allah wills, secrets and wonders beyond enumeration. And with Allah is success; there is no lord besides Him, and no worshipped other than Him. We ask Him, glorified and exalted, to make us and those we love at the time of death utterers of the testimony (kalimat al-shahāda), knowing it. May Allah bless our master Muhammad, whenever those who remember remember him and those who forget are heedless of his remembrance, and may Allah be pleased with all the companions of the Messenger of Allah and those who follow them in excellence until the Day of Judgment, and peace be upon the messengers, and praise be to Allah, the Lord of the worlds.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a combined classification and exposition. It begins by stating the three rational categories (wājib, mustaḥīl, jā’iz) that every responsible Muslim must know regarding Allah. Then it turns to the second testimony, showing that belief in Muhammad’s messengership entails belief in all previous prophets, angels, scriptures, and the Last Day, because Muhammad confirmed them. From this, the author deduces three things about prophets: (1) they must be truthful and cannot lie, otherwise they would not be trustworthy; (2) they are sinless—they cannot commit forbidden actions because they are models for teaching; (3) they may experience human accidents (like eating, illness) as these do not harm their status. After deriving these points, the author marvels at the comprehensiveness of the two testimonies despite their brevity. He explains that Islamic law made them the expression of inner faith and does not accept belief without them. He concludes by urging the intelligent believer to recite them frequently with mindfulness of their meanings, so that faith becomes deeply ingrained. The passage ends with a prayer for a good death uttering the shahada with knowledge, and with salutations and praise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the second testimony only affirms Muhammad's prophethood, and that human accidents in prophets indicate moral imperfection.
Correction: The author shows that the second testimony implicitly includes all articles of faith, and human accidents are permissible and do not harm prophetic rank.

Checkpoint
What does belief in Muhammad's messengership necessarily include according to the text?
A) Only belief in Muhammad
B) Belief in all prophets, angels, books, and the Last Day
C) Belief in angels only
D) Belief in the Last Day only

Key Takeaway
The second testimony contains a full creed, and prophets are characterized by truthfulness, sinlessness, and the permissibility of human attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you declare 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah,' do you truly believe in all the prophets, angels, books, and the Last Day? Or is your testimony hollow, disconnected from a life lived in awareness of the Final Hour?
?
The Prophet (PBUH) was sinless and truthful in every word. Is there a single teaching of his that you have taken lightly or questioned? Will you commit today to act upon his every command as if it came from Allah Himself?
?
The author says that the Prophet's human experiences increase his rank. Do you view your own trials as distractions or as opportunities to increase your rank with Allah? What would change if you saw every difficulty as a chance to rise in His sight?

Rational Judgments

The Virtue and Practice of the Shahada
Sanusi concludes by praising the shahada and urging its mindful repetition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the two testimonies concisely encompass all articles of faith, why the Sacred Law made them the expression of Islam, and the importance of reciting them with mindful contemplation.

Core Idea
The shahada is concise yet comprehensive; it is the key to faith.

After explaining the content of the two testimonies, Sanusi marvels at their comprehensiveness. He explains that Islamic law made them the verbal expression of Islam and urges believers to recite them frequently with awareness of their meanings, promising spiritual secrets. This lesson focuses on the concluding exhortation.

Guided Path
1
Read the concluding passage
Read from 'فَقَدْ بَانَ لَكَ' to the end of the supplication. Let the author's wonderment sink in.
This passage is a reflection on the shahada's comprehensiveness.
2
Note the key points
Identify: (1) the shahada contains all required beliefs, (2) it is the tarjama (expression) of Islam, (3) the command to recite it often with understanding.
The author emphasizes 'قِلَّةِ حُرُوفِهَا' and 'اشْتِمَالِهَا'.
3
Reflect on the practice
The author calls the 'āqil to repeat the shahada with presence of heart until its meaning intermingles with his flesh and blood. Consider how this applies to your own practice.
The goal is to make the shahada a living reality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بِسْمِ اللَّهِ. الْأَقْسَامُ الثَّلَاثَةُ الَّتِي يَجِبُ عَلَى الْمُكَلَّفِ مَعْرِفَتُهَا فِي حَقِّ مَوْلَانَا جَلَّ وَعَزَّ، وَهِيَ مَا يَجِبُ فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى، وَمَا يَسْتَحِيلُ، وَمَا يَجُوزُ. وَأَمَّا قَوْلُنَا مُحَمَّدٌ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَيَدْخُلُ فِيهِ الْإِيمَانُ بِسَائِرِ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ وَالْمَلَائِكَةِ وَالْكُتُبِ السَّمَاوِيَّةِ وَالْيَوْمِ الْآخِرِ، لِأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ جَاءَ بِتَصْدِيقِ جَمِيعِ ذَلِكَ كُلِّهِ، وَيُؤْخَذُ مِنْهُ وُجُوبُ صِدْقِ الرُّسُلِ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ وَاسْتِحَالَةُ الْكَذِبِ عَلَيْهِمْ، وَإِلَّا لَمْ يَكُونُوا رُسُلًا أُمَنَاءَ لِمَوْلَانَا الْعَالِمِ بِالْخَفِيَّاتِ جَلَّ وَعَزَّ، وَاسْتِحَالَةُ فِعْلِ الْمَنْهِيَّاتِ كُلِّهَا لِأَنَّهُمْ أُرْسِلُوا لِيُعَلِّمُوا النَّاسَ بِأَقْوَالِهِمْ وَأَفْعَالِهِمْ وَسُكُونِهِمْ، فَيَلْزَمُ أَنْ لَا يَكُونَ فِي جَمِيعِهَا مُخَالَفَةٌ لِأَمْرِ مَوْلَانَا جَلَّ وَعَزَّ الَّذِي اخْتَارَهُمْ عَلَى جَمِيعِ خَلْقِهِ وَأَمَّنَهُمْ عَلَى سِرِّ وَحْيِهِ، وَيُؤْخَذُ مِنْهُ جَوَازُ الْأَعْرَاضِ الْبَشَرِيَّةِ عَلَيْهِمْ، إِذْ ذَاكَ لَا يَقْدَحُ فِي رِسَالَتِهِمْ، وَعُلُوِّ مَنْزِلَتِهِمْ عِنْدَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى بَلْ ذَاكَ مِمَّا يَزِيدُ فِيهَا، فَقَدْ بَانَ لَكَ تَضَمَّنُ كَلِمَتَيِ الشَّهَادَةِ مَعَ قِلَّةِ حُرُوفِهَا لِجَمِيعِ مَا يَجِبُ عَلَى الْمُكَلَّفِ مَعْرِفَتُهُ مِنْ عَقَائِدِ الْإِيمَانِ فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى وَفِي حَقِّ رُسُلِهِ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ، وَلَعَلَّهَا لِاخْتِصَارِهَا مَعَ اشْتِمَالِهَا عَلَى مَا ذَكَرْنَاهُ جَعَلَهَا الشَّرْعُ تَرْجَمَةً عَلَى مَا فِي الْقَلْبِ مِنَ الْإِسْلَامِ، وَلَمْ يَقْبَلْ مِنْ أَحَدٍ الْإِيمَانَ إِلَّا بِهَا، فَعَلَى الْعَاقِلِ أَنْ يُكْثِرَ مِنْ ذِكْرِهَا مُسْتَحْضِرًا لِمَا احْتَوَتْ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ عَقَائِدِ الْإِيمَانِ حَتَّى يَمْتَزِجَ مَعْنَاهَا بِلَحْمِهِ وَدَمِهِ فَإِنَّهُ يَرَى لَهَا مِنَ الْأَسْرَارِ وَالْعَجَائِبِ إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى مَا لَا يَدْخُلُ تَحْتَ حَصْرٍ، وَبِاللَّهِ التَّوْفِيقُ لَا رَبَّ غَيْرُهُ وَلَا مَعْبُودَ سِوَاهُ، نَسْأَلُهُ سُبْحَانَهُ وَتَعَالَى أَنْ يَجْعَلَنَا وَأَحِبَّتَنَا عِنْدَ الْمَوْتِ نَاطِقِينَ بِكَلِمَةِ الشَّهَادَةِ عَالِمِينَ بِهَا، وَصَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَى سَيِّدِنَا مُحَمَّدٍ، كُلَّمَا ذَكَرَهُ الذَّاكِرُونَ وَغَفَلَ عَنْ ذِكْرِهِ الْغَافِلُونَ، وَرَضِيَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى عَنْ أَصْحَابِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ أَجْمَعِينَ وَالتَّابِعِينَ لَهُمْ بِإِحْسَانٍ إِلَى يَوْمِ الدِّينِ، وَسَلَامٌ عَلَى الْمُرْسَلِينَ، وَالْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ.
In the name of Allah. The three divisions that are obligatory for the legally responsible person (al-mukallaf) to know concerning our Master, may He be glorified and exalted, are: what is necessary (wājib) in His right, the Exalted, what is impossible (mustaḥīl), and what is permissible (jā’iz). And as for our statement 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace,' it includes belief in all the prophets, angels, heavenly books, and the Last Day, because he, peace and blessings be upon him, came affirming all of that. And from this is derived the necessity of the truthfulness of the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, and the impossibility of lying for them, otherwise they would not be trustworthy messengers for our Master, the Knower of hidden things, may He be glorified and exalted, and the impossibility of committing all forbidden actions because they were sent to teach people by their sayings, actions, and states, so it is necessary that there be no contradiction in all of that to the command of our Master, may He be glorified and exalted, who chose them over all His creation and entrusted them with the secret of His revelation. And from this is derived the permissibility of human accidental attributes (al-a‘rāḍ al-bashariyya) for them, for that does not detract from their messengership, but rather increases their rank with Allah, the Exalted. So it has become clear to you that the two testimonies, despite the fewness of their letters, contain all that is obligatory for the legally responsible person to know of the beliefs of faith concerning Him, the Exalted, and concerning His messengers, peace and blessings be upon them. And perhaps it is for their conciseness, with their inclusion of what we have mentioned, that the Sacred Law made them the expression (tarjama) of what is in the heart of Islam, and did not accept faith from anyone except by them. So it is upon the intelligent person (al-‘āqil) to repeat them frequently, keeping in mind the beliefs of faith they contain, until its meaning mixes with his flesh and blood, for he will see for them, if Allah wills, secrets and wonders beyond enumeration. And with Allah is success; there is no lord besides Him, and no worshipped other than Him. We ask Him, glorified and exalted, to make us and those we love at the time of death utterers of the testimony (kalimat al-shahāda), knowing it. May Allah bless our master Muhammad, whenever those who remember remember him and those who forget are heedless of his remembrance, and may Allah be pleased with all the companions of the Messenger of Allah and those who follow them in excellence until the Day of Judgment, and peace be upon the messengers, and praise be to Allah, the Lord of the worlds.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a combined classification and exposition. It begins by stating the three rational categories (wājib, mustaḥīl, jā’iz) that every responsible Muslim must know regarding Allah. Then it turns to the second testimony, showing that belief in Muhammad’s messengership entails belief in all previous prophets, angels, scriptures, and the Last Day, because Muhammad confirmed them. From this, the author deduces three things about prophets: (1) they must be truthful and cannot lie, otherwise they would not be trustworthy; (2) they are sinless—they cannot commit forbidden actions because they are models for teaching; (3) they may experience human accidents (like eating, illness) as these do not harm their status. After deriving these points, the author marvels at the comprehensiveness of the two testimonies despite their brevity. He explains that Islamic law made them the expression of inner faith and does not accept belief without them. He concludes by urging the intelligent believer to recite them frequently with mindfulness of their meanings, so that faith becomes deeply ingrained. The passage ends with a prayer for a good death uttering the shahada with knowledge, and with salutations and praise.

اختصار
ترجمة
إيمان

كلمة الشهادة

Checkpoint
According to the text, why did the Sacred Law make the shahada the expression of Islam?
A) Because it is short
B) Because it concisely contains all articles of faith
C) Because it is easy to say
D) Because it is the first pillar of Islam

Key Takeaway
The shahada is a concise yet complete summary of faith; it must be recited with understanding and frequent contemplation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the shahada, do you consciously affirm every belief it contains about Allah and His messengers, or do you just let the words pass over your tongue? What would it take for you to truly 'keep in mind the beliefs of faith' each time?
?
The shahada must 'mix with your flesh and blood'—meaning every part of you must be saturated by it. Is there any area of your life where your behavior contradicts what the shahada proclaims? What one step can you take today to align your actions with your testimony?
?
You will one day die uttering this testimony if Allah wills—but only if you have truly known it. Do you know the shahada deeply enough to face your Lord with it? What will you do today to move from mere recitation to true understanding?

The Three Rational Categories Regarding Allah
The author enumerates the three rational categories concerning Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three rational judgments (necessary, impossible, possible) that every morally responsible person must know concerning Allah.

Core Idea
The first testimony requires us to know what is necessary, impossible, and possible for Allah.

The author begins by establishing the foundational categories of divine attributes. Before delving into the details of faith, one must grasp the framework of rational judgments that apply to Allah. This passage introduces that framework.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage about the three categories once without analysing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the author uses a very compressed style here.
2
Identify the three categories
The passage presents three rational judgments: necessary (wajib), impossible (mustahil), and possible (ja'iz). Find each one and notice how the author defines them.
3
Ask: why does this matter?
Ask yourself why these three categories are the first thing a student of kalam must learn. The commentary will help you answer.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text

بسم الله. الأقسام الثلاثةِ الَّتِي يَجِبُ عَلَى الْمُكَلِّفِ مَعْرِفَتُهَا فِي حَقَّ مَوْلَانَا جَلَّ وَعَزَّ، وَهِيَ مَا يَحِبُ فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى، وَمَا يَسْتَحِيلُ، وَمَا يَجُوزُ. وَأَما قَوْلُنَا مُحَمَّدٌ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَيَدْخُلُ فِيهِ الإِيمَانُ بِسَائِرِ الأَنبِياءِ وَالْمَلائِكَةِ وَالْكُتُبِ السَّمَاوِيَّةِ وَالْيَوْمِ الآخِرِ، لأَنه عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلامُ جَاءَ بِتَصْدِيقِ جَمِيعِ ذَلِكَ كُلِّهِ، وَيُؤْخَدُ مِنْهُ وُجُوبُ صِدْقِ الرُّسُلِ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلامُ وَاسْتِحَالَةُ الكَذِبِ عَلَيْهِمْ، وَإِلا لَمْ يَكُونُوا رُسُلاً أُمَنَاءَ لِمَوْلَانَا الْعَالِمِ بِالْخَفِيَّاتِ جَلَّ وَعَزَّ وَاسْتِحَالَة فِعْلِ الْمَنْهِيَّاتِ كُلَّهَا لأَنَّهُم أُرْسِلُوا لِيُعَلِّمُوا النَّاسَ بِأَقْوَالِهِمْ، وَأَفْعَالِهِمْ وَسُكُونِهِمْ، فيلزم أن لا يَكُونَ فِي جَمِيعِهَا مُخَالَفَةٌ لأَمْرِ مَوْلانَا جَلَّ وَعَزَّ الَّذِي اخْتَارَهُمْ عَلَى جَمِيع خَلْقِهِ وَأَمَنَهُمْ عَلَى سِرٌ وَحْيِهِ، وَيُؤْخَدُ مِنْهُ جَوَارُ الْأَعْرَاضِ الْبَشَرِيَّةِ عَلَيْهِمْ، إِذْ دَاكَ لا يَقدَح فِي رِسَالَتِهِمْ، وَعُلُو مَنْزِلَتِهِمْ عِندَ الله تَعَالَى بَلْ دَاكَ مِمَّا يَزِيدُ فِيهَا ، فَقَدْ بَانَ لَكَ نَضَمَّن كُلِمَتَي الشَّهَادَةِ مَعَ قِلَةِ حُرُوفهَا لِجَمِيعِ مَا يَجِبُ عَلَى الْمُكَلِّفِ مَعْرِفَتُهُ مِنْ عَقَائِدِ الإِيمَانِ فِي حَمْهِ تَعَالَى وَفِي حَقٌّ رُسُلِهِ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ وَلَعَلَهَا لاخْتِصَارِهَا مَعَ اشتمالها على ما ذكَرنَاهُ جَعَلَهَا الشَّرْعُ تَرْجَمَة عَلَى مَا فِي الْقَلْبِ مِنَ الْإِسْلامِ، وَلَمْ يَقْبَلُ مِنْ أحد الإيمان إلا بِهَا فَعَلَى العَاقِلِ أَنْ يُكْثَرَ مِن ذِكْرِهَا مُسْتَحْضِيرا لِمَا احْتَوَتْ عَلَيْهَ مِنْ عَقَائِدِ الإِيمَانِ حَتَّى يَمتزج مَعَ مَعْنَاهَا بِلَحْمِهِ وَدَمِهِ فَإِنَّهُ يَرَى لَهَا مِنَ الأَسْرَارِ وَالْعَجَائِبِ إِنْ شَاءَ الله تَعَالَى مَا لاَ يَدْخُلُ تَحْتَ حَصْر، وَبِاللَّهِ التَّوْفِيقُ لا رَبَّ غَيْرُهُ، وَلا تَعْبُودَ سِوَاهُ، نَسْأَلُهُ سُبْحَانَهُ وتَعَالَى أَنْ يَجْعَلَنَا وَأَحِبَتَنَا عِنْدَ الْمَوْتِ نَاطِقِينَ بِكَلِمَةِ الشَّهَادَةِ عَالِمِينَ بِهَا، وَصَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَى سَيّدِنَا مُحَمَّدٍ ، كُلَّمَا دَكَرَهُ الدَّاكِرُونَ، وَغَفِلَ عَنْ ذِكْرِهِ الْغَافِلُونَ، وَرَضِيَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى عَنْ أَصْحَابِ رَسُولِ اللهِ أَجْمَعِينَ وَالتَّابِعِينَ لَهُم بِإِحْسَانٍ إِلَى يَوْمِ الدِّينِ، وَسَلَام عَلَى الْمُرْسَلِينَ، وَالْحَمْدُ اللهِ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ.
In the name of Allah. The three divisions that it is obligatory for the morally responsible person to know concerning our Lord, Mighty and Majestic: that which is necessary in His right, Exalted is He, that which is impossible, and that which is possible. As for our statement 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace,' it includes belief in all the [other] prophets, angels, heavenly books, and the Last Day, because he, peace and blessings be upon him, came confirming all of that entirely. From it is derived the obligation of the truthfulness of the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, and the impossibility of lying upon them; otherwise they would not be trustworthy messengers for our Lord, the Knower of hidden things, Mighty and Majestic. And [from it is derived] the impossibility of their committing all prohibited acts, because they were sent to teach people by their words, actions, and states of rest, so it follows that there should be no opposition in all of them to the command of our Lord, Mighty and Majestic, who chose them over all His creation and entrusted them with the secret of His revelation. From it is derived the permissibility of human accidents (al-aʿrāḍ al-bashariyya) occurring to them, for that does not detract from their messengership nor from the loftiness of their rank with Allah, Exalted is He; rather that increases them in it. It has become clear to you that the two words of testimony, despite the fewness of their letters, encompass all that is obligatory for the morally responsible person to know of the beliefs (ʿaqāʾid) of faith concerning Him, Exalted is He, and concerning the right of His messengers, peace and blessings be upon them. Perhaps because of their conciseness while including what we have mentioned, the Law made them a symbol (tarjama) for what is in the heart of Islam, and does not accept faith from anyone except with them. So it is upon the intelligent person to frequently mention them, keeping in mind what they contain of the beliefs of faith, until its meaning mixes with his flesh and blood, for he will see of their secrets and wonders, if Allah wills, that which cannot be enumerated. And Allah grants success; there is no lord besides Him, nor is any worshipped other than Him. We ask Him, glorified and exalted, to make us and our loved ones at death utterers of the testimony, knowledgeable of it. May Allah bless our master Muḥammad, whenever the rememberers remember him and the heedless neglect his remembrance. May Allah be pleased with all the companions of the Messenger of Allah and with those who follow them in righteousness until the Day of Judgment. Peace be upon the messengers, and praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the content and implications of the two testimonies of Islam: 'There is no god but Allah' and 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah.' The author explains that the first testimony encompasses three categories of divine attributes that every morally responsible person must know: what is necessarily true of Allah (wājib), what is impossible for Him (mustaḥīl), and what is possible for Him (jāʾiz). The second testimony includes belief in all prophets, angels, scriptures, and the Last Day because the Prophet Muhammad confirmed them all. From this testimony, the author derives three theological conclusions: (1) the obligation of truthfulness for all messengers and the impossibility of lying for them, otherwise they would not be trustworthy; (2) the impossibility of their committing any prohibited acts, since they were sent to teach people by example; and (3) the permissibility of normal human experiences (such as eating, sleeping, etc.) for prophets, as these do not diminish their station but rather increase it. The author then marvels at how these two short phrases contain all essential beliefs, which is why Islamic law made them the verbal testament of faith. He exhorts the reader to recite them frequently while contemplating their meaning, so that faith becomes deeply ingrained, and concludes with a prayer for a faithful end and blessings upon the Prophet and his companions.

The Second Testimony: Its Scope and Prophetic Sinlessness
The author explains the content of the second testimony and derives the obligation of truthfulness and sinlessness for prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the second testimony includes belief in all prophets, angels, books, and the Last Day, and from it derives the obligation of prophetic truthfulness and sinlessness.

Core Idea
The second testimony implies the impossibility of lying and sinning for prophets.

After establishing the categories regarding Allah, the author turns to the second testimony. He shows that this short phrase encompasses vast beliefs and logically necessitates the truthfulness and sinlessness of prophets.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage about the second testimony once without analysing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the logical deductions the author makes.
2
Identify the scope and rulings
The passage first lists what the testimony includes, then derives two rulings: truthfulness and sinlessness. Find each part.
3
Reflect on the reasoning
Ask yourself why the author argues that prophets cannot lie or sin. The commentary explains the logical necessity.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله. الأقسام الثلاثةِ الَّتِي يَجِبُ عَلَى الْمُكَلِّفِ مَعْرِفَتُهَا فِي حَقَّ مَوْلَانَا جَلَّ وَعَزَّ، وَهِيَ مَا يَحِبُ فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى، وَمَا يَسْتَحِيلُ، وَمَا يَجُوزُ. وَأَما قَوْلُنَا مُحَمَّدٌ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَيَدْخُلُ فِيهِ الإِيمَانُ بِسَائِرِ الأَنبِياءِ وَالْمَلائِكَةِ وَالْكُتُبِ السَّمَاوِيَّةِ وَالْيَوْمِ الآخِرِ، لأَنه عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلامُ جَاءَ بِتَصْدِيقِ جَمِيعِ ذَلِكَ كُلِّهِ، وَيُؤْخَدُ مِنْهُ وُجُوبُ صِدْقِ الرُّسُلِ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلامُ وَاسْتِحَالَةُ الكَذِبِ عَلَيْهِمْ، وَإِلا لَمْ يَكُونُوا رُسُلاً أُمَنَاءَ لِمَوْلَانَا الْعَالِمِ بِالْخَفِيَّاتِ جَلَّ وَعَزَّ وَاسْتِحَالَة فِعْلِ الْمَنْهِيَّاتِ كُلَّهَا لأَنَّهُم أُرْسِلُوا لِيُعَلِّمُوا النَّاسَ بِأَقْوَالِهِمْ، وَأَفْعَالِهِمْ وَسُكُونِهِمْ، فيلزم أن لا يَكُونَ فِي جَمِيعِهَا مُخَالَفَةٌ لأَمْرِ مَوْلانَا جَلَّ وَعَزَّ الَّذِي اخْتَارَهُمْ عَلَى جَمِيع خَلْقِهِ وَأَمَنَهُمْ عَلَى سِرٌ وَحْيِهِ، وَيُؤْخَدُ مِنْهُ جَوَارُ الْأَعْرَاضِ الْبَشَرِيَّةِ عَلَيْهِمْ، إِذْ دَاكَ لا يَقدَح فِي رِسَالَتِهِمْ، وَعُلُو مَنْزِلَتِهِمْ عِندَ الله تَعَالَى بَلْ دَاكَ مِمَّا يَزِيدُ فِيهَا ، فَقَدْ بَانَ لَكَ نَضَمَّن كُلِمَتَي الشَّهَادَةِ مَعَ قِلَةِ حُرُوفهَا لِجَمِيعِ مَا يَجِبُ عَلَى الْمُكَلِّفِ مَعْرِفَتُهُ مِنْ عَقَائِدِ الإِيمَانِ فِي حَمْهِ تَعَالَى وَفِي حَقٌّ رُسُلِهِ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ وَلَعَلَهَا لاخْتِصَارِهَا مَعَ اشتمالها على ما ذكَرنَاهُ جَعَلَهَا الشَّرْعُ تَرْجَمَة عَلَى مَا فِي الْقَلْبِ مِنَ الْإِسْلامِ، وَلَمْ يَقْبَلُ مِنْ أحد الإيمان إلا بِهَا فَعَلَى العَاقِلِ أَنْ يُكْثَرَ مِن ذِكْرِهَا مُسْتَحْضِيرا لِمَا احْتَوَتْ عَلَيْهَ مِنْ عَقَائِدِ الإِيمَانِ حَتَّى يَمتزج مَعَ مَعْنَاهَا بِلَحْمِهِ وَدَمِهِ فَإِنَّهُ يَرَى لَهَا مِنَ الأَسْرَارِ وَالْعَجَائِبِ إِنْ شَاءَ الله تَعَالَى مَا لاَ يَدْخُلُ تَحْتَ حَصْر، وَبِاللَّهِ التَّوْفِيقُ لا رَبَّ غَيْرُهُ، وَلا تَعْبُودَ سِوَاهُ، نَسْأَلُهُ سُبْحَانَهُ وتَعَالَى أَنْ يَجْعَلَنَا وَأَحِبَتَنَا عِنْدَ الْمَوْتِ نَاطِقِينَ بِكَلِمَةِ الشَّهَادَةِ عَالِمِينَ بِهَا، وَصَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَى سَيّدِنَا مُحَمَّدٍ ، كُلَّمَا دَكَرَهُ الدَّاكِرُونَ، وَغَفِلَ عَنْ ذِكْرِهِ الْغَافِلُونَ، وَرَضِيَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى عَنْ أَصْحَابِ رَسُولِ اللهِ أَجْمَعِينَ وَالتَّابِعِينَ لَهُم بِإِحْسَانٍ إِلَى يَوْمِ الدِّينِ، وَسَلَام عَلَى الْمُرْسَلِينَ، وَالْحَمْدُ اللهِ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ.
In the name of Allah. The three divisions that it is obligatory for the morally responsible person to know concerning our Lord, Mighty and Majestic: that which is necessary in His right, Exalted is He, that which is impossible, and that which is possible. As for our statement 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace,' it includes belief in all the [other] prophets, angels, heavenly books, and the Last Day, because he, peace and blessings be upon him, came confirming all of that entirely. From it is derived the obligation of the truthfulness of the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, and the impossibility of lying upon them; otherwise they would not be trustworthy messengers for our Lord, the Knower of hidden things, Mighty and Majestic. And [from it is derived] the impossibility of their committing all prohibited acts, because they were sent to teach people by their words, actions, and states of rest, so it follows that there should be no opposition in all of them to the command of our Lord, Mighty and Majestic, who chose them over all His creation and entrusted them with the secret of His revelation. From it is derived the permissibility of human accidents (al-aʿrāḍ al-bashariyya) occurring to them, for that does not detract from their messengership nor from the loftiness of their rank with Allah, Exalted is He; rather that increases them in it. It has become clear to you that the two words of testimony, despite the fewness of their letters, encompass all that is obligatory for the morally responsible person to know of the beliefs (ʿaqāʾid) of faith concerning Him, Exalted is He, and concerning the right of His messengers, peace and blessings be upon them. Perhaps because of their conciseness while including what we have mentioned, the Law made them a symbol (tarjama) for what is in the heart of Islam, and does not accept faith from anyone except with them. So it is upon the intelligent person to frequently mention them, keeping in mind what they contain of the beliefs of faith, until its meaning mixes with his flesh and blood, for he will see of their secrets and wonders, if Allah wills, that which cannot be enumerated. And Allah grants success; there is no lord besides Him, nor is any worshipped other than Him. We ask Him, glorified and exalted, to make us and our loved ones at death utterers of the testimony, knowledgeable of it. May Allah bless our master Muḥammad, whenever the rememberers remember him and the heedless neglect his remembrance. May Allah be pleased with all the companions of the Messenger of Allah and with those who follow them in righteousness until the Day of Judgment. Peace be upon the messengers, and praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the content and implications of the two testimonies of Islam: 'There is no god but Allah' and 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah.' The author explains that the first testimony encompasses three categories of divine attributes that every morally responsible person must know: what is necessarily true of Allah (wājib), what is impossible for Him (mustaḥīl), and what is possible for Him (jāʾiz). The second testimony includes belief in all prophets, angels, scriptures, and the Last Day because the Prophet Muhammad confirmed them all. From this testimony, the author derives three theological conclusions: (1) the obligation of truthfulness for all messengers and the impossibility of lying for them, otherwise they would not be trustworthy; (2) the impossibility of their committing any prohibited acts, since they were sent to teach people by example; and (3) the permissibility of normal human experiences (such as eating, sleeping, etc.) for prophets, as these do not diminish their station but rather increase it. The author then marvels at how these two short phrases contain all essential beliefs, which is why Islamic law made them the verbal testament of faith. He exhorts the reader to recite them frequently while contemplating their meaning, so that faith becomes deeply ingrained, and concludes with a prayer for a faithful end and blessings upon the Prophet and his companions.

Key Terms
رسول
صِدْق
كذب
عصمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets can sometimes commit minor sins or unintentional mistakes that are not sinful.
Correction: The text states that it is impossible for prophets to commit any prohibited acts, as they are models in all their sayings, actions, and states.

Checkpoint
What does the second testimony include according to the author?
A) Only belief in Muhammad
B) Belief in all prophets, angels, books, and the Last Day
C) Only belief in the Last Day
D) Only belief in angels

Key Takeaway
The second testimony encompasses belief in all prophets and also logically requires that prophets be truthful and sinless.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet ﷺ was truthful in every word and action. Is there any area of your life where you compromise on truthfulness? What specific step will you take this week to align your speech with the truth you claim to believe?
?
Prophets teach by their actions and even their states of rest. Think of a time when your private behavior contradicted the Islamic values you publicly affirm. How can you bring your 'states of rest' into obedience to Allah starting today?
?
The second testimony includes belief in all prophets. Have you neglected to learn about or respect any prophet? What practical action will you take this month to increase your love and knowledge of the entire chain of prophethood?

The Permissibility of Human Accidents for Prophets
The author states that human accidents are permissible for prophets and explains why.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that prophets may experience normal human situations (human accidents) such as eating, sleeping, etc., and that this does not detract from their prophethood.

Core Idea
Human experiences are permissible for prophets and even increase their rank.

The author continues deriving implications from the second testimony. While prophets are free from sin, they are not superhuman in every way. Normal human experiences are permitted and even enhance their station.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage about the permissibility of human accidents once without analysing it. Then read the translation.
Notice the short, precise language.
2
Understand the ruling
The passage states that human accidents are permissible (ja'iz) and do not harm prophethood. Identify the reasoning given.
3
Reflect on its significance
Ask yourself why it is important to affirm that prophets are human in these ways. The commentary will help.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text

بِكَلِمَةِ الشَّهَادَةِ عَالِمِينَ بِهَا، وَصَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَى سَيّدِنَا مُحَمَّدٍ ، كُلَّمَا دَكَرَهُ الدَّاكِرُونَ، وَغَفِلَ عَنْ ذِكْرِهِ الْغَافِلُونَ، وَرَضِيَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى عَنْ أَصْحَابِ رَسُولِ اللهِ أَجْمَعِينَ وَالتَّابِعِينَ لَهُم بِإِحْسَانٍ إِلَى يَوْمِ الدِّينِ، وَسَلَام عَلَى الْمُرْسَلِينَ، وَالْحَمْدُ اللهِ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ.
In the name of Allah. The three divisions that it is obligatory for the morally responsible person to know concerning our Lord, Mighty and Majestic: that which is necessary in His right, Exalted is He, that which is impossible, and that which is possible. As for our statement 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace,' it includes belief in all the [other] prophets, angels, heavenly books, and the Last Day, because he, peace and blessings be upon him, came confirming all of that entirely. From it is derived the obligation of the truthfulness of the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, and the impossibility of lying upon them; otherwise they would not be trustworthy messengers for our Lord, the Knower of hidden things, Mighty and Majestic. And [from it is derived] the impossibility of their committing all prohibited acts, because they were sent to teach people by their words, actions, and states of rest, so it follows that there should be no opposition in all of them to the command of our Lord, Mighty and Majestic, who chose them over all His creation and entrusted them with the secret of His revelation. From it is derived the permissibility of human accidents (al-aʿrāḍ al-bashariyya) occurring to them, for that does not detract from their messengership nor from the loftiness of their rank with Allah, Exalted is He; rather that increases them in it. It has become clear to you that the two words of testimony, despite the fewness of their letters, encompass all that is obligatory for the morally responsible person to know of the beliefs (ʿaqāʾid) of faith concerning Him, Exalted is He, and concerning the right of His messengers, peace and blessings be upon them. Perhaps because of their conciseness while including what we have mentioned, the Law made them a symbol (tarjama) for what is in the heart of Islam, and does not accept faith from anyone except with them. So it is upon the intelligent person to frequently mention them, keeping in mind what they contain of the beliefs of faith, until its meaning mixes with his flesh and blood, for he will see of their secrets and wonders, if Allah wills, that which cannot be enumerated. And Allah grants success; there is no lord besides Him, nor is any worshipped other than Him. We ask Him, glorified and exalted, to make us and our loved ones at death utterers of the testimony, knowledgeable of it. May Allah bless our master Muḥammad, whenever the rememberers remember him and the heedless neglect his remembrance. May Allah be pleased with all the companions of the Messenger of Allah and with those who follow them in righteousness until the Day of Judgment. Peace be upon the messengers, and praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds.

This passage is an exposition of the content and implications of the two testimonies of Islam: 'There is no god but Allah' and 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah.' The author explains that the first testimony encompasses three categories of divine attributes that every morally responsible person must know: what is necessarily true of Allah (wājib), what is impossible for Him (mustaḥīl), and what is possible for Him (jāʾiz). What is the ruling regarding prophets experiencing normal human conditions?
A) It is necessary
B) It is impossible
C) It is permissible

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you find yourself distancing from the prophets because you think they are too perfect to relate to? How would seeing their humanity—as the passage emphasizes—change that distance?
?
When you face a hardship or a human weakness, do you feel it diminishes your faith or rank with Allah? What does this lesson teach you about how Allah views human struggles even for His chosen ones?
?
If you truly believed that enduring human trials can increase your rank with Allah, what would you change about how you react to your next moment of pain or fatigue? Will you commit to responding with patience and trust?

The Comprehensiveness and Recitation of the Two Testimonies
The author explains the comprehensiveness of the two testimonies and urges their frequent recitation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the two testimonies encompass all essential beliefs and why frequent recitation with contemplation is encouraged.

Core Idea
The two testimonies contain the entire creed, making daily recitation a spiritual practice.

The author concludes the section by emphasizing the comprehensiveness of the two testimonies. Despite their brevity, they contain all mandatory beliefs. Therefore, the Law made them the declaration of faith. The author encourages constant remembrance with understanding.

Guided Path
1
Read the concluding passage
Read the Arabic passage from 'فَقَدْ بَانَ لَكَ' to the end once without analysing it. Then read the translation.
This passage includes a prayer, but focus on the main point first.
2
Identify the key claims
The author states that the testimonies encompass all beliefs and that the Law made them the symbol of Islam. Find these points.
3
Reflect on the practice
Consider why the author urges frequent recitation with presence of mind and heart. The commentary will help explain.
This connects to the learning objective.

بسم الله. الأقسام الثلاثةِ الَّتِي يَجِبُ عَلَى الْمُكَلِّفِ مَعْرِفَتُهَا فِي حَقَّ مَوْلَانَا جَلَّ وَعَزَّ، وَهِيَ مَا يَحِبُ فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى، وَمَا يَسْتَحِيلُ، وَمَا يَجُوزُ. وَأَما قَوْلُنَا مُحَمَّدٌ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَيَدْخُلُ فِيهِ الإِيمَانُ بِسَائِرِ الأَنبِياءِ وَالْمَلائِكَةِ وَالْكُتُبِ السَّمَاوِيَّةِ وَالْيَوْمِ الآخِرِ، لأَنه عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلامُ جَاءَ بِتَصْدِيقِ جَمِيعِ ذَلِكَ كُلِّهِ، وَيُؤْخَدُ مِنْهُ وُجُوبُ صِدْقِ الرُّسُلِ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلامُ وَاسْتِحَالَةُ الكَذِبِ عَلَيْهِمْ، وَإِلا لَمْ يَكُونُوا رُسُلاً أُمَنَاءَ لِمَوْلَانَا الْعَالِمِ بِالْخَفِيَّاتِ جَلَّ وَعَزَّ وَاسْتِحَالَة فِعْلِ الْمَنْهِيَّاتِ كُلَّهَا لأَنَّهُم أُرْسِلُوا لِيُعَلِّمُوا النَّاسَ بِأَقْوَالِهِمْ، وَأَفْعَالِهِمْ وَسُكُونِهِمْ، فيلزم أن لا يَكُونَ فِي جَمِيعِهَا مُخَالَفَةٌ لأَمْرِ مَوْلانَا جَلَّ وَعَزَّ الَّذِي اخْتَارَهُمْ عَلَى جَمِيع خَلْقِهِ وَأَمَنَهُمْ عَلَى سِرٌ وَحْيِهِ، وَيُؤْخَدُ مِنْهُ جَوَارُ الْأَعْرَاضِ الْبَشَرِيَّةِ عَلَيْهِمْ، إِذْ دَاكَ لا يَقدَح فِي رِسَالَتِهِمْ، وَعُلُو مَنْزِلَتِهِمْ عِندَ الله تَعَالَى بَلْ دَاكَ مِمَّا يَزِيدُ فِيهَا ، فَقَدْ بَانَ لَكَ نَضَمَّن كُلِمَتَي الشَّهَادَةِ مَعَ قِلَةِ حُرُوفهَا لِجَمِيعِ مَا يَجِبُ عَلَى الْمُكَلِّفِ مَعْرِفَتُهُ مِنْ عَقَائِدِ الإِيمَانِ فِي حَمْهِ تَعَالَى وَفِي حَقٌّ رُسُلِهِ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ وَلَعَلَهَا لاخْتِصَارِهَا مَعَ اشتمالها على ما ذكَرنَاهُ جَعَلَهَا الشَّرْعُ تَرْجَمَة عَلَى مَا فِي الْقَلْبِ مِنَ الْإِسْلامِ، وَلَمْ يَقْبَلُ مِنْ أحد الإيمان إلا بِهَا فَعَلَى العَاقِلِ أَنْ يُكْثَرَ مِن ذِكْرِهَا مُسْتَحْضِيرا لِمَا احْتَوَتْ عَلَيْهَ مِنْ عَقَائِدِ الإِيمَانِ حَتَّى يَمتزج مَعَ مَعْنَاهَا بِلَحْمِهِ وَدَمِهِ فَإِنَّهُ يَرَى لَهَا مِنَ الأَسْرَارِ وَالْعَجَائِبِ إِنْ شَاءَ الله تَعَالَى مَا لاَ يَدْخُلُ تَحْتَ حَصْر، وَبِاللَّهِ التَّوْفِيقُ لا رَبَّ غَيْرُهُ، وَلا تَعْبُودَ سِوَاهُ، نَسْأَلُهُ سُبْحَانَهُ وتَعَالَى أَنْ يَجْعَلَنَا وَأَحِبَتَنَا عِنْدَ الْمَوْتِ نَاطِقِينَ بِكَلِمَةِ الشَّهَادَةِ عَالِمِينَ بِهَا، وَصَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَى سَيّدِنَا مُحَمَّدٍ ، كُلَّمَا دَكَرَهُ الدَّاكِرُونَ، وَغَفِلَ عَنْ ذِكْرِهِ الْغَافِلُونَ، وَرَضِيَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى عَنْ أَصْحَابِ رَسُولِ اللهِ أَجْمَعِينَ وَالتَّابِعِينَ لَهُم بِإِحْسَانٍ إِلَى يَوْمِ الدِّينِ، وَسَلَام عَلَى الْمُرْسَلِينَ، وَالْحَمْدُ اللهِ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ.
In the name of Allah. The three divisions that it is obligatory for the morally responsible person to know concerning our Lord, Mighty and Majestic: that which is necessary in His right, Exalted is He, that which is impossible, and that which is possible. As for our statement 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace,' it includes belief in all the [other] prophets, angels, heavenly books, and the Last Day, because he, peace and blessings be upon him, came confirming all of that entirely. From it is derived the obligation of the truthfulness of the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, and the impossibility of lying upon them; otherwise they would not be trustworthy messengers for our Lord, the Knower of hidden things, Mighty and Majestic. And [from it is derived] the impossibility of their committing all prohibited acts, because they were sent to teach people by their words, actions, and states of rest, so it follows that there should be no opposition in all of them to the command of our Lord, Mighty and Majestic, who chose them over all His creation and entrusted them with the secret of His revelation. From it is derived the permissibility of human accidents (al-aʿrāḍ al-bashariyya) occurring to them, for that does not detract from their messengership nor from the loftiness of their rank with Allah, Exalted is He; rather that increases them in it. It has become clear to you that the two words of testimony, despite the fewness of their letters, encompass all that is obligatory for the morally responsible person to know of the beliefs (ʿaqāʾid) of faith concerning Him, Exalted is He, and concerning the right of His messengers, peace and blessings be upon them. Perhaps because of their conciseness while including what we have mentioned, the Law made them a symbol (tarjama) for what is in the heart of Islam, and does not accept faith from anyone except with them. So it is upon the intelligent person to frequently mention them, keeping in mind what they contain of the beliefs of faith, until its meaning mixes with his flesh and blood, for he will see of their secrets and wonders, if Allah wills, that which cannot be enumerated. And Allah grants success; there is no lord besides Him, nor is any worshipped other than Him. We ask Him, glorified and exalted, to make us and our loved ones at death utterers of the testimony, knowledgeable of it. May Allah bless our master Muḥammad, whenever the rememberers remember him and the heedless neglect his remembrance. May Allah be pleased with all the companions of the Messenger of Allah and with those who follow them in righteousness until the Day of Judgment. Peace be upon the messengers, and praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the content and implications of the two testimonies of Islam: 'There is no god but Allah' and 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah.' The author explains that the first testimony encompasses three categories of divine attributes that every morally responsible person must know: what is necessarily true of Allah (wājib), what is impossible for Him (mustaḥīl), and what is possible for Him (jāʾiz). The second testimony includes belief in all prophets, angels, scriptures, and the Last Day because the Prophet Muhammad confirmed them all. From this testimony, the author derives three theological conclusions: (1) the obligation of truthfulness for all messengers and the impossibility of lying for them, otherwise they would not be trustworthy; (2) the impossibility of their committing any prohibited acts, since they were sent to teach people by example; and (3) the permissibility of normal human experiences (such as eating, sleeping, etc.) for prophets, as these do not diminish their station but rather increase it. The author then marvels at how these two short phrases contain all essential beliefs, which is why Islamic law made them the verbal testament of faith. He exhorts the reader to recite them frequently while contemplating their meaning, so that faith becomes deeply ingrained, and concludes with a prayer for a faithful end and blessings upon the Prophet and his companions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The two testimonies are just a simple phrase without deeper content.
Correction: The passage emphasizes that they contain all essential beliefs of faith.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why did the Law make the two testimonies the symbol of Islam?
A) Because they are short
B) Because they contain all essential beliefs
C) Because they are easy to memorize
D) Because they are beautiful

Key Takeaway
The two testimonies encapsulate all necessary beliefs, and frequent recitation with understanding is a key spiritual practice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the two testimonies daily, do you consciously remember that they contain all the beliefs required of you, or has it become a hollow repetition? What practical change can you make starting today to ensure your recitation is mindful?
?
If at the moment of death you were asked to utter the shahada with perfect knowledge and sincerity, would you be confident that it has mixed 'with your flesh and blood'? What deficiencies in your current understanding or practice might hinder that, and what step will you take this week to strengthen your connection to its meaning?
?
The Law does not accept faith except through the two testimonies. Have you ever truly examined whether your inner convictions align with every implication of 'La ilaha illa Allah' and 'Muhammadun Rasul Allah'? Write down one area of your life where your actions contradict this declaration, and commit to repenting from it today.
